   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of countries by carbon dioxide emissions</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       This article is about only carbon dioxide. For the carbon dioxide equivalent of all greenhouse gases combined, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_greenhouse_gas_emissions" title="List of countries by greenhouse gas emissions">List of countries by greenhouse gas emissions</a>.
      </div>

      <p>This is a <b>list of sovereign states and territories by <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> emissions</b> due to certain forms of human activity, based on the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.sec.gov/edgar.shtml">EDGAR database</a> created by <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> and <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Environmental_Assessment_Agency" title="Netherlands Environmental Assessment Agency">Netherlands Environmental Assessment Agency</a> released in 2018. The following table lists the 1990, 2005 and 2017 annual <span class="nowrap"><span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br>2</span></span></span> emissions estimates (in Megatonnes of <span class="nowrap"><span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br>2</span></span></span> per year) along with a list of calculated emissions per km² (in tonnes of <span class="nowrap"><span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br>2</span></span></span> per year) and emissions per capita (in tonnes of <span class="nowrap"><span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br>2</span></span></span> per year). </p>
      <p>The data only consider carbon dioxide emissions from the burning of <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels" class="mw-redirect" title="Fossil fuels">fossil fuels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cement_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Cement industry">cement manufacture</a>, but not emissions from <a href="/wiki/Land_use,_land-use_change_and_forestry" class="mw-redirect" title="Land use, land-use change and forestry">land use, land-use change and forestry</a>. Emissions from international shipping or <a href="/wiki/Bunker_fuel" class="mw-redirect" title="Bunker fuel">bunker fuels</a> are also not included in national figures,<sup id="cite_ref-Schrooten2_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schrooten2-1">[1]</a></sup> which can make a large difference for small countries with important ports. When carbon dioxide emissions from land-use change are factored in, the majority of carbon emissions since 1905 occurred in Asia, Central and Southern America, reflecting the fact that developed nations cleared their forests in earlier centuries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Land-use factors have contributed nearly a third of total cumulative anthropogenic emissions of carbon dioxide since 1850, and until as recently as 1965 was actually a greater source of emissions than the combustion of fossil fuels and production of cement.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> The methodology for the calculations is public.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The top 10 largest emitter countries account for 67.6% of the world total. Since 2006, China has been emitting more <span class="nowrap"><span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br>2</span></span></span> than any other country,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> but all being equal, to make a fair comparison of contributions, emissions in terms of CO2 per person have to be made.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> When looking at <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_carbon_dioxide_emissions_per_capita" title="List of countries by carbon dioxide emissions per capita"> China’s figures are about one eighth of the biggest <span class="nowrap"><span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br>2</span></span></span> emitter per person</a> and half of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Production-based_emissions_of_greenhouse_gases" class="mw-redirect" title="Production-based emissions of greenhouse gases">Territorial-based emissions</a> do not account for global trade, where emissions may be imported or exported in the form of traded goods. Accordingly, a proportion of the <span class="nowrap"><span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br>2</span></span></span> produced and reported in Asia and Eastern Europe is for the production of goods consumed in Western Europe and North America.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the review of the scientific literature conducted by the <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</a> (IPCC), carbon dioxide is the most important <a href="/wiki/Anthropogenic_greenhouse_gas" class="mw-redirect" title="Anthropogenic greenhouse gas">anthropogenic greenhouse gas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The other major <a href="/wiki/Anthropogenic_greenhouse_gases" class="mw-redirect" title="Anthropogenic greenhouse gases">anthropogenic greenhouse gases</a> (<a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">methane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nitrous_oxide" title="Nitrous oxide">nitrous oxide</a> (N<sub>2</sub>O) and some <a href="/wiki/Fluorinated_gases" title="Fluorinated gases">fluorinated gases</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sulfur_hexafluoride" title="Sulfur hexafluoride">sulfur hexafluoride</a> (SF<sub>6</sub>), <a href="/wiki/Hydrofluorocarbons" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydrofluorocarbons">hydrofluorocarbons</a> (HFCs), and <a href="/wiki/Perfluorocarbons" class="mw-redirect" title="Perfluorocarbons">perfluorocarbons</a> (PFCs))<sup id="cite_ref-grubb_kyoto_protocol_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grubb_kyoto_protocol-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>147</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Environmental_issues:_essential_primary_sources._14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Environmental_issues:_essential_primary_sources.-14">[14]</a></sup>), are not included in the following list, nor are humans emissions of <a href="/wiki/Water_vapor" title="Water vapor">water vapor</a> (H<sub>2</sub>O), the most important <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.britannica.com/science/greenhouse-gas">greenhouse gases</a>, as they are negligible compared to naturally occurring quantities.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Space-based_measurements_of_carbon_dioxide" title="Space-based measurements of carbon dioxide">Space-based measurements of carbon dioxide</a> should allow independent monitoring in the mid-2020s.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Per_capita_CO2_emissions">Per capita <span class="nowrap"><span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br>2</span></span></span> emissions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_carbon_dioxide_emissions&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Per capita CO2 emissions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_carbon_dioxide_emissions_per_capita" title="List of countries by carbon dioxide emissions per capita">List of countries by carbon dioxide emissions per capita</a>

Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://ourworldindata.org/co2-and-other-greenhouse-gas-emissions#per-capita-co2-emissions">the original</a> on 4 July 2019. <q>The key drawback of measuring the total national emissions is that it takes no account of the nation's population size. China is currently the world’s largest emitter and is also home to the largest population. This is expected, but this figure does not take into account China’s construction at home and abroad where new projects all over the world that are taking place as part of China’s Belt and Road Initiative. To make a population based comparison of contributions, we can only compare emissions in terms of CO2 emitted per person, but this does not include the CO2 emitted as part of these valuable infrastructure projects world wide.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Our+World+in+Data&amp;rft.atitle=CO%E2%82%82+and+other+Greenhouse+Gas+Emissions&amp;rft.date=2017-05-11&amp;rft.aulast=Roser&amp;rft.aufirst=Max&amp;rft.au=Ritchie%2C+Hannah&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fourworldindata.org%2Fco2-and-other-greenhouse-gas-emissions%23per-capita-co2-emissions&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+countries+by+carbon+dioxide+emissions" class="Z3988"></span>
